256<h2 id="bodyTitle">

257Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment (PDQ®)–Patient Version</h2>

264

265 <h3>

266General Information About Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

267

268 <div id="_129" class="pdq-sections">

269

270 <div id="_section_129" class="pdq-sections">

271<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

272<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-nhl-treatment-pdq">

273Go to Health Professional Version</a>

274</div>

275<div class="key-points">

276<h3 id="_129_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

277Key Points</h3>

278<div id="_kp_section_129_1">

279<ul>

280<li>

281Non-Hodgkin lymphoma is a disease in which malignant

282 (cancer) cells form in the lymph system.</li>

283<li>

284Non-Hodgkin lymphoma can be indolent or aggressive.</li>

285<li>

286Older age, being male, and having a weakened immune system can increase the risk of

287 non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

288<li>

289Signs and symptoms of non-Hodgkin lymphoma include swollen lymph nodes, fever,

290 drenching night sweats, weight loss, and fatigue. </li>

291<li>

292Tests that examine the lymph system and other parts of the body are used to diagnose and stage non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

293<li>

294Certain factors affect prognosis (chance

295 of recovery) and treatment options.</li>

296</ul>

297</div>

298</div>

299<section id="_130">

300<h3 id="_131" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

301Non-Hodgkin lymphoma is a disease in which malignant

302 (cancer) cells form in the lymph system.</h3>

303<p id="_132" tabindex="-1">

304<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

305Non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

306 is a type of

307 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

308cancer</a>

309 that forms in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

310lymph system</a>

311. The lymph system is part of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

312immune system</a>

313. It helps protect the body from <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

314infection</a>

315 and disease.</p>

316<p id="_475" tabindex="-1">

317The lymph system is made up of the following:</p>

318<div class="pdq-content-list">

319<ul id="_476">

320<li>

321<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46305&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046305&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

322Lymph</a>

323: Colorless, watery <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

324fluid</a>

325 that travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

326lymph vessels</a>

327 and carries <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45765&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045765&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

328lymphocytes</a>

329 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45993&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045993&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

330white blood cells</a>

331). There are three types of lymphocytes:<div class="pdq-content-list">

332<ul id="_477">

333<li>

334<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44953&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044953&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

335B lymphocytes</a>

336 that make <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

337antibodies</a>

338 to help fight infection. Also called B cells. Most types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma begin in B lymphocytes.</li>

339<li>

340<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

341T lymphocytes</a>

342 that help B lymphocytes make the antibodies that help fight infection. Also called T cells.</li>

343<li>

344<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44062&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044062&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

345Natural killer cells</a>

346 that attack cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

347cells</a>

354<li>

426<section id="_376">

427<h3 id="_377" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

428Non-Hodgkin lymphoma can be indolent or aggressive.</h3>

429<p id="_378" tabindex="-1">

430Non-Hodgkin lymphoma grows and spreads at different rates and can be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46355&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046355&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

431indolent</a>

432 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46053&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046053&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

433aggressive</a>

434. Indolent lymphoma tends to grow and spread slowly, and has few <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

435signs</a>

436 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

437symptoms</a>

438. Aggressive lymphoma grows and spreads quickly, and has signs and symptoms that can be severe. The treatments for indolent and aggressive lymphoma are different.</p>

439<p id="_397" tabindex="-1">

440This summary is about the following types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma:</p>

441<section id="_379">

442<p id="_453" tabindex="-1">

443<strong>

444Indolent non-Hodgkin lymphomas</strong>

445</p>

446<div class="pdq-content-list">

447<ul id="_398" class="pdq-address-block">

448<li>

449<strong>

450<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=428287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000428287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

451Follicular lymphoma</a>

452.</strong>

453 Follicular lymphoma is the most common type of indolent non-Hodgkin lymphoma. It is a very slow-growing type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma that begins in B lymphocytes. It affects the lymph nodes and may spread to the bone marrow or spleen. Most patients with follicular lymphoma are age 50 years and older when they are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

454diagnosed</a>

455. Follicular lymphoma may go away without treatment. The patient is closely watched for signs or symptoms that the disease has come back. Treatment is needed if signs or symptoms occur after the cancer disappeared or after initial cancer treatment. Sometimes follicular lymphoma can become a more aggressive type of lymphoma, such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

456diffuse large B-cell lymphoma</a>

457.</li>

458<li>

459<strong>

460<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409750&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409750&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

461Lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma</a>

462.</strong>

463 In most cases of lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma, B lymphocytes that are turning into <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46230&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046230&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

464plasma cells</a>

465 make large amounts of a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

466protein</a>

467 called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=411378&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000411378&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

468monoclonal</a>

469 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45725&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045725&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

470immunoglobulin</a>

471 M (IgM) antibody. High levels of IgM antibody in the blood cause the blood <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45839&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045839&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

472plasma</a>

473 to thicken. This may cause signs or symptoms such as trouble seeing or hearing, heart problems, shortness of breath, headache, dizziness, and numbness or tingling of the hands and feet. Sometimes there are no signs or symptoms of lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma. It may be found when a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=688783&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000688783&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

474blood test</a>

475 is done for another reason. Lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma often spreads to the bone marrow, lymph nodes, and spleen. Patients with lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma should be checked for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44139&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044139&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

476hepatitis C virus</a>

477 infection. It is also called Waldenstr&#246;m macroglobulinemia.</li>

478<li>

479<strong>

480<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=543124&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000543124&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

482.</strong>

The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

489 disease, and those with high <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

532<strong>

533Mediterranean <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

538 called <em>

539Campylobacter jejuni</em>

540. This type of lymphoma is also called immunoproliferative small intestinal disease.</li>

541<li>

542<strong>

543<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=467863&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000467863&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

544Splenic</a>

545 marginal zone lymphoma.</strong>

546 This type of marginal zone lymphoma begins in the spleen and may spread to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46011&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046011&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

547peripheral blood</a>

548 and bone marrow. The most common sign of this type of splenic marginal zone lymphoma is a spleen that is larger than normal.</li>

549</ul>

550</div>

551</li>

552<li>

553<strong>

554<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=748354&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000748354&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

555Primary</a>

556 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

557cutaneous</a>

558 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45552&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045552&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

559anaplastic large cell lymphoma</a>

560.</strong>

561 This type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma is in the skin only. It can be a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45614&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045614&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

562benign</a>

563 (not cancer) <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44502&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044502&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

564nodule</a>

565 that may go away on its own or it can spread to many places on the skin and need treatment.</li>

566</ul>

568</section>

569<section id="_392">

570<p id="_454" tabindex="-1">

571<strong>

572Aggressive non-Hodgkin lymphomas</strong>

573</p>

574<div class="pdq-content-list">

575<ul id="_399" class="pdq-address-block">

576<li>

577<strong>

578Diffuse large B-cell lymphoma.</strong>

579 Diffuse large B-cell lymphoma is the most common type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma. It grows quickly in the lymph nodes and often the spleen, liver, bone marrow, or other organs are also affected. Signs and symptoms of diffuse large B-cell lymphoma may include <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

580fever</a>

581, drenching night sweats, and weight loss. These are also called B symptoms.<div class="pdq-content-list">

582<ul id="_408">

583<li>

584<strong>

585Primary mediastinal large B-cell lymphoma.</strong>

586 This type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma is a type of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

587diffuse large B-cell lymphoma</a>

588. It is marked by the overgrowth of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=344349&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000344349&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

589fibrous</a>

590 (scar-like) lymph tissue. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

591tumor</a>

592 most often forms behind the breastbone. It may press on the airways and cause coughing and trouble breathing. Most patients with primary mediastinal large B-cell lymphoma are women who are age 30 to 40 years.</li>

593</ul>

594</div>

595</li>

596<li>

597<strong>

598<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44238&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044238&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

599Follicular large cell lymphoma</a>

600, stage III.</strong>

601 Follicular large cell lymphoma, stage III, is a very rare type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma. Treatment of this type of follicular lymphoma is more like treatment of aggressive NHL than of indolent NHL. </li>

602<li>

603<strong>

604Anaplastic large cell lymphoma.</strong>

605 Anaplastic large cell lymphoma is a type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma that usually begins in T lymphocytes. The cancer cells also have a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

606marker</a>

607 called CD30 on the surface of the cell. <p id="_409" tabindex="-1">

608There are two types of anaplastic large cell lymphoma:</p>

609<div class="pdq-content-list">

610<ul id="_410">

611<li>

612<strong>

613Cutaneous anaplastic large cell lymphoma.</strong>

614 This type of anaplastic large cell lymphoma mostly affects the skin, but other parts of the body may also be affected. Signs of cutaneous anaplastic large cell lymphoma include one or more bumps or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=390317&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000390317&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

615ulcers</a>

616 on the skin. This type of lymphoma is rare and indolent. </li>

617<li>

618<strong>

619<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

620Systemic</a>

621 anaplastic large cell lymphoma.</strong>

622 This type of anaplastic large cell lymphoma begins in the lymph nodes and may affect other parts of the body. This type of lymphoma is more aggressive. Patients may have a lot of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45591&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045591&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

623anaplastic</a>

624 lymphoma <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=641114&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000641114&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

625kinase</a>

626 (ALK) protein inside the lymphoma cells. These patients have a better <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

627prognosis</a>

628 than patients who do not have extra ALK protein. Systemic anaplastic large cell lymphoma is more common in children than adults. For more information, see <a href="/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq">

629Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment</a>

630.</li>

634<li>

635<strong>

638 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44439&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044439&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

651 in the tumor cells. Sometimes hemophagocytic <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

652syndrome</a>

653 occurs (a serious <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

654condition</a>

655 in which there are too many active histiocytes and T cells that cause severe <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44042&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044042&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

657 in the body). Treatment to suppress the immune system is needed. This type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma is not common in the United States. </li>

658<li>

659<strong>

660<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

663 Lymphomatoid granulomatosis mostly affects the lungs. 665, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

667. In lymphomatoid granulomatosis, cancer invades the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

668blood vessels</a>

669 and kills tissue. Because the cancer may spread to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

670brain</a>

671, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

672intrathecal chemotherapy</a>

673 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

675 to the brain is given.</li>

676<li>

677<strong>

678<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=346464&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000346464&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

679Angioimmunoblastic T-cell lymphoma</a>

680.</strong>

681 This type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma begins in T cells. Swollen lymph nodes are a common sign. Other signs may include a skin rash, fever, weight loss, or drenching night sweats. There may also be high levels of gamma globulin (antibodies) in the blood. Patients may also have opportunistic infections because their immune systems are weakened.</li>

682<li>

683<strong>

684<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=405873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000405873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

685Peripheral T-cell lymphoma</a>

686.</strong>

687 Peripheral T-cell lymphoma begins in mature T lymphocytes. This type of T lymphocyte matures in the thymus <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46386&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046386&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

688gland</a>

689 and travels to other lymphatic sites in the body such as the lymph nodes, bone marrow, and spleen. There are three subtypes of peripheral T-cell lymphoma:<div class="pdq-content-list">

690<ul id="_412">

691<li>

692<strong>

693Hepatosplenic T-cell lymphoma.</strong>

694 This is an uncommon type of peripheral T-cell lymphoma that occurs mostly in young men. It begins in the liver and spleen and the cancer cells also have a T-cell <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

695receptor</a>

696 called gamma/delta on the surface of the cell. </li>

697<li>

698<strong>

699<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

700Subcutaneous</a>

701 panniculitis-like T-cell lymphoma.</strong>

702 Subcutaneous panniculitis-like T-cell lymphoma begins in the skin or mucosa. It may occur with hemophagocytic syndrome (a serious condition in which there are too many active histiocytes and T cells that cause severe inflammation in the body). Treatment to suppress the immune system is needed.</li>

703<li>

704<strong>

705Enteropathy-type <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44046&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044046&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

706intestinal</a>

707 T-cell lymphoma.</strong>

708 This type of peripheral T-cell lymphoma occurs in the small <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46500&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046500&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

709bowel</a>

710 of patients with untreated <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=377726&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000377726&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

711celiac disease</a>

712 (an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45722&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045722&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

713immune response</a>

714 to gluten that causes <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46014&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046014&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

715malnutrition</a>

716). Patients who are diagnosed with celiac disease in childhood and stay on a gluten-free <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

717diet</a>

718 rarely develop enteropathy-type intestinal T-cell lymphoma.</li>

721</li>

722<li>

723<strong>

724Intravascular large B-cell lymphoma.</strong>

725 This type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma affects blood vessels, especially the small blood vessels in the brain, kidney, lung, and skin. Signs and symptoms of intravascular large B-cell lymphoma are caused by blocked blood vessels. It is also called intravascular lymphomatosis.</li>

726<li>

727<strong>

728<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45203&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045203&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

729Burkitt lymphoma</a>

730.</strong>

731 Burkitt lymphoma is a type of B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma that grows and spreads very quickly. It may affect the jaw, bones of the face, bowel, kidneys, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46687&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046687&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

732ovaries</a>

733, or other organs. There are three main types of Burkitt lymphoma (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=776371&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000776371&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

734endemic</a>

735, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=339347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000339347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

736sporadic</a>

737, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

738immunodeficiency</a>

739 related). Endemic Burkitt lymphoma commonly occurs in Africa and is linked to the Epstein-Barr virus, and sporadic Burkitt lymphoma occurs throughout the world. Immunodeficiency-related Burkitt lymphoma is most often seen in patients who have <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45950&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045950&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

740AIDS</a>

741. Burkitt lymphoma may spread to the brain and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

742spinal cord</a>

743 and treatment to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=439419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000439419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

744prevent</a>

745 its spread may be given. Burkitt lymphoma occurs most often in children and young adults. For more information, see <a href="/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq">

746Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment</a>

747. Burkitt lymphoma is also called diffuse small noncleaved-cell lymphoma.</li>

748<li>

749<strong>

750<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=597158&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000597158&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

751Lymphoblastic lymphoma</a>

752.</strong>

753 Lymphoblastic lymphoma may begin in T cells or B cells, but it usually begins in T cells. In this type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma, there are too many <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=302475&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000302475&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

754lymphoblasts</a>

755 (immature white blood cells) in the lymph nodes and the thymus gland. These lymphoblasts may spread to other places in the body, such as the bone marrow, brain, and spinal cord. Lymphoblastic lymphoma is most common in teenagers and young adults. It is a lot like <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

756acute lymphoblastic leukemia</a>

757 (lymphoblasts are mostly found in the bone marrow and blood). For more information, see <a href="/types/leukemia/patient/adult-all-treatment-pdq">

758Adult Acute Lymphoblastic Leukemia Treatment</a>

759.</li>

760<li>

761<strong>

762<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

763T-cell leukemia/lymphoma</a>

764.</strong>

765 T-cell leukemia/lymphoma is caused by the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269420&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269420&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

766human T-cell leukemia virus type 1</a>

767 (HTLV-1). Signs include bone and skin <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46324&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046324&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

768lesions</a>

769, high blood <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45632&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045632&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

770calcium</a>

771 levels, and lymph nodes, spleen, and liver that are larger than normal. </li>

772<li>

773<strong>

774<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445048&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445048&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

775Mantle cell lymphoma</a>

776.</strong>

777 Mantle cell lymphoma is a type of B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma that usually occurs in middle-aged or older adults. It begins in the lymph nodes and spreads to the spleen, bone marrow, blood, and sometimes the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46408&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046408&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

778esophagus</a>

779, stomach, and intestines. Patients with mantle cell lymphoma have too much of a protein called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=729820&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000729820&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

780cyclin-D1</a>

781 or a certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

782gene</a>

783 change in the lymphoma cells. In some patients who do not have signs or symptoms of lymphoma, delaying the start of treatment does not affect the prognosis.</li>

784<li>

785<strong>

786<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

787Posttransplantation lymphoproliferative disorder</a>

788.</strong>

789 This disease occurs in patients who have had a heart, lung, liver, kidney, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46254&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046254&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

790pancreas</a>

791 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46631&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046631&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

792transplant</a>

793 and need lifelong <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45728&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045728&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

794immunosuppressive therapy</a>

795. Most posttransplant lymphoproliferative disorders affect the B cells and have Epstein-Barr virus in the cells. Lymphoproliferative disorders are often treated like cancer. </li>

796<li>

797<strong>

798True <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=373019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000373019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

799histiocytic lymphoma</a>

800.</strong>

801 This is a rare, very aggressive type of lymphoma. It is not known whether it begins in B cells or T cells. It does not respond well to treatment with standard <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

802chemotherapy</a>

803.</li>

804<li>

805<strong>

806<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=455144&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000455144&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

807Primary effusion lymphoma</a>

808.</strong>

809 Primary effusion lymphoma begins in B cells that are found in an area where there is a large build-up of fluid, such as the areas between the lining of the lung and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44996&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044996&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

810chest wall</a>

811 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45843&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045843&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

812pleural effusion</a>

813), the sac around the heart and the heart (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

814pericardial effusion</a>

815), or in the abdominal <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

816cavity</a>

817. There is usually no tumor that can be seen. This type of lymphoma often occurs in patients who are infected with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44985&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044985&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

818HIV</a>

819.</li>

820<li>

821<strong>

822<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=776368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000776368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

823Plasmablastic lymphoma</a>

824.</strong>

825 Plasmablastic lymphoma is a type of large B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma that is very aggressive. It is most often seen in patients with HIV infection.</li>

826</ul>

827</div>

829</section>

830<section id="_140">

831<h3 id="_141" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

832Older age, being male, and having a weakened immune system can increase the risk of

833 non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</h3>

834<p id="_142" tabindex="-1">

835Anything that increases a person's chance of getting a disease is called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

836risk factor</a>

837. Not every person with one or more of these risk factors will develop non-Hodgkin lymphoma, and it can develop in people who don't have any known risk factors. Talk with your doctor if you think you may be at risk. </p>

838<p id="_413" tabindex="-1">

839These and other risk factors may increase the risk of certain types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma:</p>

840<div class="pdq-content-list">

841<ul id="_143">

842<li>

843Being older, male, or White.</li>

844<li>

845Having one of the following medical conditions that weakens the immune system:<div class="pdq-content-list">

846<ul id="_144" class="list-dash">

847<li>

848An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

849inherited</a>

850 immune <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=407758&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000407758&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

851disorder</a>

852 (such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=455335&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000455335&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

853hypogammaglobulinemia</a>

854 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=539110&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000539110&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

855Wiskott-Aldrich syndrome</a>

856).</li>

857<li>

858An autoimmune disease (such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=455398&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000455398&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

859rheumatoid arthritis</a>

860, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44219&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044219&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

861psoriasis</a>

862, or Sj&#246;gren syndrome).</li>

863<li>

864HIV/AIDS.</li>

865<li>

866Human T-lymphotrophic virus type I or Epstein-Barr virus infection.</li>

867<li>

868<em>

869Helicobacter pylori</em>

870 infection.</li>

871</ul>

872</div>

873</li>

874<li>

875Taking <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45727&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045727&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

876immunosuppressant</a>

877 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

878drugs</a>

879 after an organ transplant.</li>

880</ul>

881</div>

882</section>

883<section id="_145">

884<h3 id="_146" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

885Signs and symptoms of non-Hodgkin lymphoma include swollen lymph nodes, fever,

886 drenching night sweats, weight loss, and fatigue. </h3>

887<p id="_147" tabindex="-1">

888These signs and symptoms may be caused by non-Hodgkin

889 lymphoma or by other conditions. Check with your doctor if you have any of the

890 following:</p>

891<div class="pdq-content-list">

892<ul id="_148">

893<li>

894Swelling in the lymph nodes in the neck, underarm,

895 groin, or stomach.</li>

896<li>

897Fever for no known reason.</li>

898<li>

899Drenching night sweats.</li>

900<li>

901Feeling very tired.</li>

902<li>

903Weight loss for no known reason.</li>

904<li>

905Skin rash or itchy skin.</li>

906<li>

907Pain in the chest, abdomen, or bones for no known reason.</li>

908</ul>

909</div>

910<p id="_411" tabindex="-1">

911When fever, drenching night sweats, and weight loss occur together, this group of symptoms is called B symptoms. </p>

912<p id="_415" tabindex="-1">

913Other signs and symptoms of non-Hodgkin lymphoma may occur and depend on the following:

914

915</p>

916<div class="pdq-content-list">

917<ul id="_416">

918<li>

919Where the cancer forms in the body.</li>

920<li>

921The size of the tumor.</li>

922<li>

923How fast the tumor grows.

924</li>

925</ul>

926</div>

927</section>

928<section id="_149">

929<h3 id="_150" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

930Tests that examine the lymph system and other parts of the body are used to diagnose and stage non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</h3>

931<p id="_151" tabindex="-1">

932In addition to asking about your <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

933personal</a>

934 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

935family health history</a>

936 and doing a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

937physical exam</a>

938, your doctor may perform the following tests and procedures:</p>

939<div class="pdq-content-list">

940<ul id="_152">

941<li>

942<strong>

943<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45107&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045107&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

944Complete blood count</a>

945 (CBC)</strong>

946: A procedure in which a sample of blood is drawn and checked for the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

947<ul id="_24" class="list-dash">

948<li>

949The number of red blood cells, white blood cells, and platelets.</li>

950<li>

951The amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

952hemoglobin</a>

953 (the protein that carries <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000538149&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

954oxygen</a>

955) in the red blood cells.</li>

956<li>

957The portion of the sample made up of red blood cells.</li>

958</ul>

959</div>

960<figure id="figure_490" class="image-center">

961<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/526546.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

962Enlarge</a>

963<img id="_490" alt="Complete blood count (CBC); left panel shows blood being drawn from a vein on the inside of the elbow using a tube attached to a syringe; right panel shows a laboratory test tube with blood cells separated into layers: plasma, white blood cells, platelets, and red blood cells." title="Complete blood count (CBC); left panel shows blood being drawn from a vein on the inside of the elbow using a tube attached to a syringe; right panel shows a laboratory test tube with blood cells separated into layers: plasma, white blood cells, platelets, and red blood cells." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/526546-750.jpg">

964<figcaption class="caption-container">

965Complete blood count (CBC). Blood is collected by inserting a needle into a vein and allowing the blood to flow into a tube. The blood sample is sent to the laboratory and the red blood cells, white blood cells, and platelets are counted. The CBC is used to test for, diagnose, and monitor many different conditions.</figcaption>

966</figure>

967</li>

968<li>

969<strong>

970<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304685&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304685&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

971Blood chemistry studies</a>

972</strong>

973: A procedure in which a blood sample is checked to measure the amounts of certain substances released into the blood by

974 organs and tissues in the body. An unusual (higher or lower than normal) amount of a substance can be a sign

975 of disease.</li>

976<li>

977<strong>

978<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354465&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354465&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

979LDH</a>

980 test</strong>

981: A procedure in which a blood sample is checked to measure the amount of lactic dehydrogenase. An increased amount of LDH in the blood may be a sign of tissue damage, lymphoma, or other diseases.</li>

982<li>

983<strong>

984<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46146&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046146&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

985Hepatitis B</a>

986 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44139&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044139&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

987hepatitis C</a>

988 test</strong>

989: A procedure in which a sample of blood is checked to measure the amounts of hepatitis B virus-specific <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

990antigens</a>

991 and/or antibodies and the amounts of hepatitis C virus-specific antibodies. These antigens or antibodies are called markers. Different markers or combinations of markers are used to determine whether a patient has a hepatitis B or C infection, has had a prior infection or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

992vaccination</a>

993, or is susceptible to infection. Patients who have been treated for hepatitis B virus in the past need continued <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=454803&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000454803&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

994monitoring</a>

995 to check if it has <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=683532&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000683532&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

996reactivated</a>

997. Knowing whether a person has hepatitis B or C may help plan treatment.</li>

998<li>

999<strong>

1000<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=759626&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000759626&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1001HIV test</a>

1002</strong>

1003: A test to measure the level of HIV antibodies in a sample of blood. Antibodies are made by the body when it is invaded by a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=698772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000698772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1004foreign</a>

1005 substance. A high level of HIV antibodies may mean the body has been infected with HIV.</li>

1006<li>

1007<strong>

1008<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1009CT scan</a>

1010 (CAT scan)</strong>

1011:

1012 A procedure that makes a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the neck, chest, abdomen, pelvis, and lymph nodes, taken from different angles. The pictures are made by a computer linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1013x-ray</a>

1014 machine. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1015dye</a>

1016 may be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1017injected</a>

1018 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1019vein</a>

1020 or swallowed to help the organs or tissues show up more clearly. This procedure is also called computed tomography, computerized tomography, or computerized axial tomography.</li>

1021<li>

1022<strong>

1023<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46140&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046140&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1024PET scan</a>

1025 (positron

1026 emission tomography scan)</strong>

1027: A procedure to find <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1028malignant</a>

1029 tumor cells in the body. A small amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1030radioactive</a>

1031 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1032glucose</a>

1033 (sugar) is injected into a vein. The PET <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1034scanner</a>

1035 rotates around the body and makes a picture of where glucose is being used in the body. Malignant tumor cells show up brighter in the picture because they are more active and take up more glucose than normal cells do.</li>

1036<li>

1037 <strong>

1038<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46505&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046505&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1039Bone marrow aspiration</a>

1040 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46506&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046506&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1041biopsy</a>

1042</strong>

1043: The removal of bone marrow and a small piece of bone by inserting a needle into the hipbone or breastbone. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1044pathologist</a>

1045 views the bone marrow and bone under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1046microscope</a>

1047 to look for signs of cancer.<figure id="figure_310" class="image-center">

1048<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/554337.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1049Enlarge</a>

1050<img id="_310" alt="Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy; drawing shows a patient lying face down on a table and a bone marrow needle being inserted into the hip bone. Inset shows the bone marrow needle being inserted through the skin into the bone marrow of the hip bone." title="Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy; drawing shows a patient lying face down on a table and a bone marrow needle being inserted into the hip bone. 1051<figcaption class="caption-container">

1052Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy. After a small area of skin is numbed, a bone marrow needle is inserted into the patient&#8217;s hip bone. Samples of blood, bone, and bone marrow are removed for examination under a microscope.</figcaption>

1053</figure>

1054</li>

1055<li>

1056<strong>

1057 Lymph node biopsy</strong>

1058: The

1059 removal of all or part of a lymph node. A pathologist views the tissue under a microscope to check for cancer cells. One of the following types of biopsies may be done: <div class="pdq-content-list">

1060<ul id="_154" class="list-dash">

1061<li>

1062<strong>

1063<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1064Excisional

1065 biopsy</a>

1066</strong>

1067: The removal of an entire lymph node. </li>

1068<li>

1069<strong>

1070<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1071Incisional

1072 biopsy</a>

1073</strong>

1074: The removal of part of a lymph node.</li>

1075<li>

1076<strong>

1077<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45657&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045657&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1078Core biopsy</a>

1079</strong>

1080: The removal of part of a lymph node using a wide needle. </li>

1081</ul>

1082</div>

1083</li>

1084</ul>

1085</div>

1086<p id="_319" tabindex="-1">

1087If cancer is found, the following tests may be done to study the cancer cells:

1088

1089</p>

1090<div class="pdq-content-list">

1091<ul id="_320">

1092<li>

1093<strong>

1094<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1095Immunohistochemistry</a>

1096</strong>

1097: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1098laboratory test</a>

1099 that uses antibodies to check for certain antigens (markers) in a sample of a patient&#8217;s tissue. The antibodies are usually linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1100enzyme</a>

1101 or a fluorescent dye. After the antibodies bind to a specific antigen in the tissue sample, the enzyme or dye is activated, and the antigen can then be seen under a microscope. This type of test is used to help diagnose cancer and to help tell one type of cancer from another type of cancer.</li>

1102<li>

1103<strong>

1104<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1105Cytogenetic analysis</a>

1106</strong>

1107: A laboratory test in which the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1108chromosomes</a>

1109 of cells in a sample of blood or bone marrow are counted and checked for any changes, such as broken, missing, rearranged, or extra chromosomes. Changes in certain chromosomes may be a sign of cancer. Cytogenetic analysis is used to help diagnose cancer, plan treatment, or find out how well treatment is working.</li>

1110<li>

1111<strong>

1112<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=341450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000341450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1113Immunophenotyping</a>

1114</strong>

1115: A laboratory test that uses antibodies to identify cancer cells based on the types of antigens or markers on the surface of the cells. This test is used to help diagnose specific types of lymphoma.</li>

1116<li>

1117<strong>

1118<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460228&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460228&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1119FISH</a>

1120 (fluorescence in situ hybridization)</strong>

1121: A laboratory test used to look at and count genes or chromosomes in cells and tissues. Pieces of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1122DNA</a>

1123 that contain fluorescent dyes are made in the laboratory and added to a sample of a patient&#8217;s cells or tissues. When these dyed pieces of DNA attach to certain genes or areas of chromosomes in the sample, they light up when viewed under a fluorescent microscope. The FISH test is used to help diagnose cancer and help plan treatment.</li>

1124</ul>

1125</div>

1126<p id="_417" tabindex="-1">

1127Other tests and procedures may be done depending on the signs and symptoms seen and where the cancer forms in the body.</p>

1128</section>

1129<section id="_155">

1130<h3 id="_156" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1131Certain factors affect prognosis (chance

1132 of recovery) and treatment options.</h3>

1133<p id="_260" tabindex="-1">

1134The prognosis and treatment options depend on the following:</p>

1135<div class="pdq-content-list">

1136<ul id="_261">

1137<li>

1138The patient's signs and symptoms, including whether or not they have B symptoms (fever for no known reason, weight loss for no known reason, or drenching night sweats).</li>

1139<li>

1140The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1141stage</a>

1142 of the cancer (the size of the cancer tumors and whether the cancer has spread to other parts of the body or lymph nodes).</li>

1143<li>

1144The type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </li>

1145<li>

1146The amount of lactate dehydrogenase (LDH) in the blood.</li>

1147<li>

1148Whether there are certain changes in the genes.</li>

1149<li>

1150The patient&#8217;s age, sex, and

1151 general health.</li>

1152<li>

1153Whether the lymphoma is newly diagnosed, continues to grow during treatment, or has <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45862&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045862&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1154recurred</a>

1155 (come back).</li>

1156</ul>

1157</div>

1158<p id="_275" tabindex="-1">

1159For non-Hodgkin lymphoma during pregnancy, treatment options also depend on:</p>

1160<div class="pdq-content-list">

1161<ul id="_276">

1162<li>

1163The wishes of the patient.</li>

1164<li>

1165Which trimester of pregnancy the patient is in.</li>

1166<li>

1167Whether the baby can be delivered early.</li>

1168</ul>

1169</div>

1170<p id="_277" tabindex="-1">

1171Some types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma spread more quickly than

1172 others do. Most non-Hodgkin lymphomas that occur during pregnancy are

1173 aggressive. Delaying treatment

1174 of aggressive lymphoma until after the baby is born may lessen the mother's chance of survival. Immediate

1175 treatment is often recommended, even during pregnancy. </p>

1176</section>

1177</div>

1178

1179 </div>
