1182

1183 <h3>

1184Stages of Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

1185

1186 <div id="_158" class="pdq-sections">

1187

1188 <div id="_section_158" class="pdq-sections">

1189<div class="key-points">

1190<h3 id="_158_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1191Key Points</h3>

1192<div id="_kp_section_158_2">

1193<ul>

1194<li>

1195After non-Hodgkin lymphoma has been diagnosed, tests are done to find out

1196 whether cancer cells have spread within the lymph

1197 system or to other parts of the body.

1198 </li>

1199<li>

1200There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</li>

1201<li>

1202The following stages are used for non-Hodgkin

1203 lymphoma:<ul>

1204<li>

1205Stage I</li>

1206<li>

1207Stage II</li>

1208<li>

1209Stage III </li>

1210<li>

1211Stage IV</li>

1212</ul>

1213</li>

1214<li>

1215Non-Hodgkin lymphomas may be grouped for treatment according to whether the cancer is indolent or aggressive, whether affected lymph nodes are next to each other in the body, and whether the cancer is newly diagnosed or recurrent.</li>

1216<li>

1217Non-Hodgkin lymphoma can recur (come back) after it has been treated.</li>

1218</ul>

1219</div>

1220</div>

1221<section id="_159">

1222<h3 id="_160" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1223After non-Hodgkin lymphoma has been diagnosed, tests are done to find out

1224 whether cancer cells have spread within the lymph

1225 system or to other parts of the body.

1226 </h3>

1227<p id="_161" tabindex="-1">

1228The process used to find out the type of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1229cancer</a>

1230 and if cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1231cells</a>

1232

1233 have spread within the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1234lymph system</a>

1235 or to other parts of the body is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1236staging</a>

1237. The

1238 information gathered from the staging process determines the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1239stage</a>

1240 of the

1241 disease. It is important to know the stage of the disease in order to plan treatment. The results of the <a href="/types/lymphoma/patient/adult-nhl-treatment-pdq#_150">

1242tests and procedures</a>

1243 done to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1244diagnose</a>

1245 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1246non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1247 are used to help make decisions about treatment.</p>

1248<p id="_418" tabindex="-1">

1249The following tests and procedures may also be used in the staging

1250 process:</p>

1251<div class="pdq-content-list">

1252<ul id="_163">

1253<li>

1254<strong>

1255<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1256MRI</a>

1257 (magnetic

1258 resonance imaging) with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=597153&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000597153&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1259gadolinium</a>

1260</strong>

1261: A procedure that uses a magnet, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1262radio waves</a>

1263, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1264brain</a>

1265 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1266spinal cord</a>

1267. A substance called gadolinium is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1268injected</a>

1269 into the patient through a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1270vein</a>

1271. The gadolinium collects around the cancer cells so they show up brighter in the picture. This procedure is also called nuclear magnetic resonance imaging (NMRI).</li>

1272<li>

1273<strong>

1274<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1275Lumbar puncture</a>

1276</strong>

1277: A procedure used to collect <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1278cerebrospinal fluid</a>

1279 (CSF) from the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=396787&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000396787&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1280spinal column</a>

1281. This is done by placing a needle between two bones in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1282spine</a>

1283 and into the CSF around the spinal cord and removing a sample of the fluid. The sample of CSF is checked under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1284microscope</a>

1285 for signs that the cancer has spread to the brain and spinal cord. This procedure is also called an LP or spinal tap. <figure id="figure_322" class="image-center">

1286<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/503953.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1287Enlarge</a>

1288<img id="_322" alt="Lumbar puncture; drawing shows a patient lying in a curled position on a table and a spinal needle (a long, thin needle) being inserted into the lower back. Inset shows a close-up of the spinal needle inserted into the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the lower part of the spinal column." title="Lumbar puncture; drawing shows a patient lying in a curled position on a table and a spinal needle (a long, thin needle) being inserted into the lower back. 1289<figcaption class="caption-container">

1290Lumbar puncture. A patient lies in a curled position on a table. After a small area on the lower back is numbed, a spinal needle (a long, thin needle) is inserted into the lower part of the spinal column to remove cerebrospinal fluid (CSF, shown in blue). The fluid may be sent to a laboratory for testing.</figcaption>

1291</figure>

1292</li>

1293</ul>

1294</div>

1295<p id="_284" tabindex="-1">

1296For <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1297pregnant</a>

1298 women with non-Hodgkin lymphoma, staging tests and procedures that protect the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46400&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046400&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1299fetus</a>

1300 from the harms of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1301radiation</a>

1302 are used. These tests and procedures include MRI (without contrast), lumbar puncture, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1303ultrasound</a>

1304. </p>

1306<section id="_302">

1307<h3 id="_303" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1308There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</h3>

1309<p id="_302_md_69" tabindex="-1">

1310Cancer can spread through <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1311tissue</a>

1312, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1313lymph system</a>

1314, and the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1315blood</a>

1316:</p>

1317<div class="pdq-content-list">

1318<ul id="_302_md_70">

1319<li>

1320Tissue. The cancer spreads from where it began by growing into nearby areas.

1321</li>

1322<li>

1323Lymph system. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the lymph system. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1324lymph vessels</a>

1325 to other parts of the body.

1326</li>

1327<li>

1328Blood. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the blood. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1329blood vessels</a>

1330 to other parts of the body.

1331</li>

1332</ul>

1333</div>

1334</section>

1472Stage IV adult lymphoma. Cancer (a) has spread throughout one or more organs outside the lymph system; or (b) is found in two or more groups of lymph nodes that are either above the diaphragm or below the diaphragm and in one organ that is outside the lymph system and not near the affected lymph nodes; or (c) is found in groups of lymph nodes above the diaphragm and below the diaphragm and in any organ that is outside the lymph system; or (d) is found in the liver, bone marrow, more than one place in the lung, or cerebrospinal fluid (CSF). 1512<section id="_182">

1513<h3 id="_183" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1514Non-Hodgkin lymphomas may be grouped for treatment according to whether the cancer is indolent or aggressive, whether affected lymph nodes are next to each other in the body, and whether the cancer is newly diagnosed or recurrent.</h3>

1515<p id="_414" tabindex="-1">

1516For more information on the types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1517indolent</a>

1518 (slow-growing) and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1519aggressive</a>

1520 (fast-growing) non-Hodgkin lymphoma, see the <a href="/types/lymphoma/patient/adult-nhl-treatment-pdq#_376">

1521General Information</a>

1522 section.</p>

1523<p id="_186" tabindex="-1">

1524Non-Hodgkin lymphoma can also be described as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=350356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000350356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1525contiguous</a>

1526 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=350357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000350357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1527noncontiguous</a>

1528:</p>

1529<div class="pdq-content-list">

1530<ul id="_187">

1531<li>

1532Contiguous lymphomas: <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1533Lymphomas</a>

1534 in which the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1535lymph nodes</a>

1536 with cancer are next

1537 to each other.</li>

1538<li>

1539 Noncontiguous lymphomas: Lymphomas in which the lymph nodes with cancer

1540 are not next to each other, but are on the same side of the

1541 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1542diaphragm</a>

1543.</li>

1547<section id="_314">

1548<h3 id="_315" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1549Non-Hodgkin lymphoma can recur (come back) after it has been treated.</h3>

1550<p id="_316" tabindex="-1">

1551 The lymphoma may come back

1552 in the lymph system or in other parts of the body. Indolent lymphoma may come back as

1553 aggressive lymphoma. Aggressive

1554 lymphoma may come back as indolent lymphoma.</p>

1555</section>

1569<h3 id="_190_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1570Key Points</h3>

1571<div id="_kp_section_190_3">

1572<ul>

1573<li>

1574There are different types of treatment for patients with non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </li>

1575<li>

1576Patients with non-Hodgkin lymphoma should have their treatment

1577 planned by a team of health care providers who are experts in treating lymphomas.</li>

1578<li>

1579Treatment for non-Hodgkin lymphoma may cause side effects.</li>

1580<li>

1581The following types of treatment are used:<ul>

1582<li>

1583Radiation therapy

1584 </li>

1585<li>

1586Chemotherapy </li>

1589<li>

1594Watchful waiting

1595 </li>

1597Antibiotic therapy</li>

1598<li>

1599Surgery</li>

1600<li>

1601Stem cell transplant</li>

1602</ul>

1603</li>

1604<li>

1605New types of treatment are being tested in clinical

1606 trials.<ul>

1607<li>

1608Vaccine therapy</li>

1609</ul>

1610</li>

1611<li>

1612Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</li>

1613<li>

1614Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</li>

1615<li>

1616Follow-up tests may be needed.</li>

1617</ul>

1620<section id="_191">

1621<h3 id="_192" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1622There are different types of treatment for patients with non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </h3>

1623<p id="_193" tabindex="-1">

1624Different types of treatment are available for patients with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1625non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1626. Some treatments are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1627standard</a>

1628 (the currently used treatment), and some

1629 are being tested in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1630clinical trials</a>

1631.

1632 A treatment clinical trial is a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1633research study</a>

1634 meant to help

1635 improve current treatments or obtain information on new treatments for patients

1636 with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1637cancer</a>

1638. When clinical trials show that a new treatment is better than the

1639 standard treatment, the new

1640 treatment may become the standard treatment. Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment.</p>

1641<p id="_285" tabindex="-1">

1642For <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1643pregnant</a>

1644 women with non-Hodgkin lymphoma, treatment is carefully chosen to protect the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46400&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046400&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1645fetus</a>

1646. Treatment decisions are based on the mother&#8217;s wishes, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1647stage</a>

1648 of the non-Hodgkin lymphoma, and the trimester of the pregnancy. The treatment plan may change as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1649signs</a>

1650 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1651symptoms</a>

1652, cancer, and pregnancy change. Choosing the most appropriate cancer treatment is a decision that ideally involves the patient, family, and health care team.

1653</p>

1795<section id="_195">

1796<h3 id="_196" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1797The following types of treatment are used:</h3>

1798<section id="_197">

1799<h4 id="_198" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1800Radiation therapy

1801 </h4>

1802<p id="_199" tabindex="-1">

1803Radiation therapy is a cancer treatment that uses high-energy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1804x-rays</a>

1805 or other types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1806radiation</a>

1807 to kill cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1808cells</a>

1809 or keep them from growing. </p>

1810<p id="_506" tabindex="-1">

1811<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1812External radiation therapy</a>

1813 uses a machine outside the body to send radiation toward the area of the body with cancer. Sometimes <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1814total-body irradiation</a>

1815 is given before a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1816stem cell transplant</a>

1817.</p>

1902<img id="_455" alt="Intrathecal chemotherapy; drawing shows the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the brain and spinal cord, and an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). Top section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs into the Ommaya reservoir. Bottom section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs directly into the cerebrospinal fluid in the lower part of the spinal column." title="Intrathecal chemotherapy; drawing shows the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the brain and spinal cord, and an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). Top section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs into the Ommaya reservoir. 1903<figcaption class="caption-container">

1904Intrathecal chemotherapy. Anticancer drugs are injected into the intrathecal space, which is the space that holds the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF, shown in blue). There are two different ways to do this. One way, shown in the top part of the figure, is to inject the drugs into an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). The other way, shown in the bottom part of the figure, is to inject the drugs directly into the CSF in the lower part of the spinal column, after a small area on the lower back is numbed. </figcaption>

1905</figure>

1906<p id="_295" tabindex="-1">

1907When a pregnant woman is treated with chemotherapy for non-Hodgkin lymphoma, the fetus cannot be protected from being exposed to chemotherapy. Some chemotherapy regimens may cause birth defects if given in the first trimester.</p>

1961<img id="_467" alt="CAR T-cell therapy; drawing of blood being removed from a vein in a patient&#8217;s arm to get T cells. Also shown is a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) being made in the laboratory; the gene for CAR is inserted into the T cells and then millions of CAR T cells are grown. Drawing also shows the CAR T cells being given to the patient by infusion and binding to antigens on the cancer cells and killing them." title="CAR T-cell therapy; drawing of blood being removed from a vein in a patient&#8217;s arm to get T cells. Also shown is a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) being made in the laboratory; the gene for CAR is inserted into the T cells and then millions of CAR T cells are grown. Drawing also shows the CAR T cells being given to the patient by infusion and binding to antigens on the cancer cells and killing them." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/774647-750.jpg">

1962<figcaption class="caption-container">

1963CAR T-cell therapy. A type of treatment in which a patient&#8217;s T cells (a type of immune cell) are changed in the laboratory so they will bind to cancer cells and kill them. Blood from a vein in the patient&#8217;s arm flows through a tube to an apheresis machine (not shown), which removes the white blood cells, including the T cells, and sends the rest of the blood back to the patient. Then, the gene for a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) is inserted into the T cells in the laboratory. Millions of the CAR T cells are grown in the laboratory and then given to the patient by infusion. The CAR T cells are able to bind to an antigen on the cancer cells and kill them.</figcaption>

1964</figure>

As a cancer treatment, these <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1991antibodies</a>

1992 can attach to a specific target on cancer cells or other cells that may help cancer cells grow. The antibodies are able to then kill the cancer cells, block their growth, or keep them from spreading. Monoclonal antibodies are given by <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45738&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045738&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1993infusion</a>

1994. They may be used alone or to carry drugs, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2133<h4 id="_344" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2134Plasmapheresis</h4>

2135<p id="_345" tabindex="-1">

2136If the blood becomes thick with extra antibody proteins and affects <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476484&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476484&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2137circulation</a>

2138, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2139plasmapheresis</a>

2140 is done to remove extra <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45839&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045839&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2141plasma</a>

2142 and antibody proteins from the blood. In this procedure, blood is removed from the patient and sent through a machine that separates the plasma (the liquid part of the blood) from the blood cells. The patient's plasma contains the unneeded antibodies and is not returned to the patient. The normal blood cells are returned to the bloodstream along with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2143donated</a>

2144 plasma or a plasma replacement. Plasmapheresis does not keep new antibodies from forming. </p>

2176<h4 id="_370" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2178<p id="_371" tabindex="-1">

2179<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2186<p id="_374" tabindex="-1">

2187The type of surgery used depends on where the lymphoma formed in the body:</p>

2188<div class="pdq-content-list">

2231<section id="_213">

2232<h4 id="_214" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2233Stem cell transplant</h4>

2234<p id="_215" tabindex="-1">

2235Stem cell transplant is a method of giving high <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2236doses</a>

2237 of chemotherapy and/or total-body irradiation and then replacing blood-forming cells destroyed by the cancer treatment. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46598&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046598&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2238Stem cells</a>

2239 (immature blood cells) are removed from the blood or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2240bone marrow</a>

2241 of the patient (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270733&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270733&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2242autologous transplant</a>

2243) or a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2244donor</a>

2245 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270732&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270732&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2246allogeneic transplant</a>

2247) and are frozen and stored. After the chemotherapy and/or radiation therapy is completed, the stored stem cells are thawed and given back to the patient through an infusion. These reinfused stem cells grow into (and restore) the body&#8217;s blood cells.</p>

2248<figure id="figure_456" class="image-center">

2249<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/765030.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

Blood is collected from a vein in the arm and flows through a machine that removes the stem cells; the remaining blood is returned to a vein in the other arm. (Panel 2): Drawing of a health care provider giving a patient treatment to kill blood-forming cells. Chemotherapy is given to the patient through a catheter in the chest. (Panel 3): Drawing of stem cells being given to the patient through a catheter in the chest." title="Stem cell transplant; (Panel 1): Drawing of stem cells being removed from a patient or donor. 2252<figcaption class="caption-container">

2253Stem cell transplant. (Step 1): Blood is taken from a vein in the arm of the donor. The patient or another person may be the donor. The blood flows through a machine that removes the stem cells. Then the blood is returned to the donor through a vein in the other arm. (Step 2): The patient receives chemotherapy to kill blood-forming cells. The patient may receive radiation therapy (not shown). (Step 3): The patient receives stem cells through a catheter placed into a blood vessel in the chest.</figcaption>

2254</figure>

2267.</p>

2268<section id="_268">

2269<h4 id="_269" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2270Vaccine therapy</h4>

2271<p id="_270" tabindex="-1">

2272<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=386223&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000386223&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2273Vaccine therapy</a>

2274 is a cancer treatment that uses a substance or group of substances to stimulate the immune system to find the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2275tumor</a>

2276 and kill it.</p>

2278</section>

2279<section id="_304">

2280<h3 id="_305" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2281Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</h3>

2282<p id="_304_md_23" tabindex="-1">

2283For some patients, taking part in a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2284clinical trial</a>

2285 may be the best treatment choice. Clinical trials are part of the cancer research process. Clinical trials are done to find out if new cancer treatments are safe and effective or better than the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2286standard treatment</a>

2287.</p>

2288<p id="_304_md_24" tabindex="-1">

2289Many of today's standard treatments for cancer are based on earlier clinical trials. Patients who take part in a clinical trial may receive the standard treatment or be among the first to receive a new treatment.</p>

2290<p id="_304_md_25" tabindex="-1">

2291Patients who take part in clinical trials also help improve the way cancer will be treated in the future. Even when clinical trials do not lead to effective new treatments, they often answer important questions and help move research forward.</p>

2292</section>

2293<section id="_306">

2294<h3 id="_307" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2295Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</h3>

2296<p id="_306_md_29" tabindex="-1">

2297Some clinical trials only include patients who have not yet received treatment. Other trials test treatments for patients whose cancer has not gotten better. There are also clinical trials that test new ways to stop cancer from <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2298recurring</a>

2299 (coming back) or reduce the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2300side effects</a>

2301 of cancer treatment.</p>

2302<p id="_306_md_30" tabindex="-1">

2303Clinical trials are taking place in many parts of the country. Information about clinical trials supported by NCI can be found on NCI&#8217;s <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

2304clinical trials search</a>

2305 webpage. Clinical trials supported by other organizations can be found on the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

2306ClinicalTrials.gov</a>

2307 website.</p>

2308</section>

2314diagnose</a>

2316stage</a>

2317 of the cancer may be repeated. Some tests will be repeated in order to see how well the treatment is working. Decisions about whether to continue, change, or stop treatment may be based on the results of these tests.</p>

The results of these tests can show if your <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2320condition</a>

2321 has changed or if the cancer has <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2322recurred</a>

2323 (come back). These tests are sometimes called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2324follow-up</a>

2325 tests or check-ups.</p>

Monoclonal antibody therapy may be given afterwards as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45768&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045768&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2956Treatment of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2957indolent

2958 lymphoma</a>

2959 that comes back as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2960aggressive lymphoma</a>

2961 depends on the type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma and may include radiation therapy as palliative therapy to relieve symptoms and improve quality of life. Treatment of aggressive lymphoma that comes back as indolent lymphoma may include chemotherapy.</p>

2995<p id="_292" tabindex="-1">

2996

2997Women who have

2998 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46355&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046355&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2999indolent</a>

3000 (slow-growing)

3001 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3002non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

3003 during <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3004pregnancy</a>

3005 may be treated with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45942&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045942&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3011<section id="_358">

3012<h3 id="_358_toc">

3013Aggressive Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma During Pregnancy</h3>

3014<p id="_359" tabindex="-1">

3015Treatment of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045588&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3016aggressive</a>

3017

3018 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3019non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

3020 during <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3021pregnancy</a>

3023<div class="pdq-content-list">

3024<ul id="_360">

3025<li>

3026Treatment given right away based on the type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma to increase the mother's chance of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3027survival</a>

3028. Treatment may include <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45650&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045650&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3029combination chemotherapy</a>

3030 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45525&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045525&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3031rituximab</a>

3032.</li>

3033<li>

3034Early delivery of the baby followed by treatment based on the type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

3035<li>

3036If in the first trimester of pregnancy, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46290&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046290&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

3037medical oncologists</a>

3038 may advise ending the pregnancy so that treatment may begin. Treatment depends on the type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

3123 <h3>

3124About This PDQ Summary</h3>

3125

3126 <div id="_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

3127

3128 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

3129<section id="_AboutThis_2">

3130<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

3131About PDQ</h3>

3132<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

3133Physician Data Query (PDQ) is the National Cancer Institute's (NCI's) comprehensive cancer information database. The PDQ database contains summaries of the latest published information on cancer prevention, detection, genetics, treatment, supportive care, and complementary and alternative medicine. Most summaries come in two versions. The health professional versions have detailed information written in technical language. The patient versions are written in easy-to-understand, nontechnical language. Both versions have cancer information that is accurate and up to date and most versions are also available in <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/espanol/publicaciones/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/espanol/publicaciones/pdq">

3134Spanish</a>

3135.</p>

3136<p id="_AboutThis_4" tabindex="-1">

3137PDQ is a service of the NCI. The NCI is part of the National Institutes of Health (NIH). NIH is the federal government&#8217;s center of biomedical research. The PDQ summaries are based on an independent review of the medical literature. They are not policy statements of the NCI or the NIH.</p>

3138</section>

3139<section id="_AboutThis_5">

3140<h3 id="_AboutThis_5_toc">

3141Purpose of This Summary</h3>

3142<p id="_AboutThis_6" tabindex="-1">

3143This PDQ cancer information summary has current information about the treatment of adult non-Hodgkin lymphoma. It is meant to inform and help patients, families, and caregivers. It does not give formal guidelines or recommendations for making decisions about health care.</p>

3144</section>

3145<section id="_AboutThis_7">

3146<h3 id="_AboutThis_7_toc">

3147Reviewers and Updates</h3>

3148<p id="_AboutThis_8" tabindex="-1">

3149Editorial Boards write the PDQ cancer information summaries and keep them up to date. These Boards are made up of experts in cancer treatment and other specialties related to cancer. The summaries are reviewed regularly and changes are made when there is new information. The date on each summary ("Updated") is the date of the most recent change.

3150</p>

3151<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

3152The information in this patient summary was taken from the health professional version, which is reviewed regularly and updated as needed, by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

3153PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

3154.

3155</p>

3156</section>

3157<section id="_AboutThis_10">

3158<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

3159Clinical Trial Information</h3>

3160<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

3161A clinical trial is a study to answer a scientific question, such as whether one treatment is better than another. Trials are based on past studies and what has been learned in the laboratory. Each trial answers certain scientific questions in order to find new and better ways to help cancer patients. During treatment clinical trials, information is collected about the effects of a new treatment and how well it works. If a clinical trial shows that a new treatment is better than one currently being used, the new treatment may become "standard." Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment.

3162</p>

3163<p id="_AboutThis_12" tabindex="-1">

3164Clinical trials can be found online at <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

3165NCI's website</a>

3166. For more information, call the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/contact-center" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/contact-center">

3167Cancer Information Service</a>

3168 (CIS), NCI's contact center, at 1-800-4-CANCER (1-800-422-6237).

3169</p>

3170</section>

It cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless the whole summary is shown and it is updated regularly. However, a user would be allowed to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks in the following way: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;

3176</p>
